Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1075;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 17;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 816;
    client_max_body_size 1762304;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 0;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

	 No Anti-CSRF tokens were found in a HTML submission form.
A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1682;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 58;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1657;
    client_max_body_size 2093056;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'https://*.google.com';";
        }
    }

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 944;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 114;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1996;
    client_max_body_size 1117184;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.3.3;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 737;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 52;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1046;
    client_max_body_size 1247232;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1712;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 87;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1414;
    client_max_body_size 579584;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1204;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 49;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 560128;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low
Alert →

This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1792;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 15;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1858;
    client_max_body_size 1467392;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.3.3;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1951;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 109;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 993;
    client_max_body_size 2042880;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By nginx/1.17.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy.

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1231;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 117;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1827;
    client_max_body_size 1120256;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By nginx/1.17.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 0;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'https://*.google.com';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. * Manually resetting nginx to stopped state

        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.3.3;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1862;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 109;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 536;
    client_max_body_size 977920;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }

    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. * Manually resetting nginx to stopped state

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy.

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1066;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 95;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1473;
    client_max_body_size 1811456;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 0;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1336;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1700;
    client_max_body_size 1190912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

	 <form action="../form" method="post" enctype="multipart/form-data"> 
	 No Anti-CSRF tokens were found in a HTML submission form.
A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low
Alert →
	 http://www.exampletfm.com/test/upload.html 
	  
	 The Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1204;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 49;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 560128;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1336;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 1190912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy.

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1336;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 23;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 1190912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1336;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1700;
    client_max_body_size 1190912;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1336;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 52;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1046;
    client_max_body_size 1190912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1922;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 50;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1125;
    client_max_body_size 1647616;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }

            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;

            add_header Server caddy;

            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1951;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 109;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 993;
    client_max_body_size 2041856;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By nginx/1.17.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 737;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 52;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1046;
    client_max_body_size 1247232;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1204;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 48;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 560128;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server nginx/1.16.0;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1712;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 88;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 1190912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1697;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 88;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 554;
    client_max_body_size 1088512;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By Django2.2;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

	 http://www.exampletfm.com/test/upload.html 
	 <form action="../form" method="post" enctype="multipart/form-data"> 
	 No Anti-CSRF tokens were found in a HTML submission form.
A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy.

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1335;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1125;
    client_max_body_size 1647616;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1712;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 87;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1414;
    client_max_body_size 579584;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

	 No Anti-CSRF tokens were found in a HTML submission form.
A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy.

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 944;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 114;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1996;
    client_max_body_size 1117184;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.3.3;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server apache;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 0;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1336;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 1190912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.3.3;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy.

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1335;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1125;
    client_max_body_size 1647616;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1712;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 1190912;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options DENY;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

    worker_connections 1712;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 87;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 553;
    client_max_body_size 1089536;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;

        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 1;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'https://*.google.com';";
        }
    }

pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;

    worker_connections 1335;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1125;
    client_max_body_size 1647616;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";

            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";

    }

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low

user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1336;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 87;
    disable_symlinks on;
    autoindex off;
    send_timeout 1;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1414;
    client_max_body_size 579584;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options SAMEORIGIN;
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection 0;
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. 
	 Low
Alert →
	 http://www.exampletfm.com/test/upload.html

This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1335;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 22;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1125;
    client_max_body_size 1647616;
    server_tokens off;
    gzip off;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/5.6.8;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options "";
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'self'; frame-ancestors 'self';";
        }
    }
}

Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:
    * The victim has an active session on the target site.
    * The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.
    * The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy. * Manually resetting nginx to stopped state

Configuration → 
user nginx;
pid /var/run/nginx.pid;
worker_processes 4;
daemon on;
error_log /tmp/nginx-error.log warn;
events {
    worker_connections 1205;
}
http {
    include /etc/nginx/mime.types;
    default_type application/octet-stream;
    access_log /tmp/nginx-access.log;
    sendfile on;
    keepalive_timeout 49;
    disable_symlinks off;
    autoindex on;
    send_timeout 0;
    large_client_header_buffers 4 1769;
    client_max_body_size 560128;
    server_tokens on;
    gzip on;
    log_format my_tracking $request_body;
    resolver 8.8.8.8 valid=30s;
    server {
        server_name www.exampletfm.com;
        listen 80;
        error_page 500 502 503 504 /50x.html;
        location ^~ /assets/public/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location ^~ /assets/assets/ {
            deny all;
        }
        location /form {
            access_log /tmp/access.log my_tracking;
        }
        location / {
            root /tester/site/;
            index index.html index.htm;
            add_header X-Frame-Options "ALLOW-FROM http://www.exampletfm.com/";
            add_header X-Powered-By PHP/7.2.1;
            add_header X-Content-Type-Options nosniff;
            add_header Server caddy;
            add_header X-XSS-Protection "1; mode=block";
            add_header Content-Security-Policy "default-src 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none';";
        }
    }
}

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy.
